Municipal Government Requests Central Government to Restrict the Import of Foreign Rice 103

Executive Yuan Will Submit for Discussion at Next Meeting

According to the Dagong News Agency, since the drought last year caused poor harvests, rice merchants in various places have been purchasing foreign rice from Saigon, Siam, Xiaojiao, etc., for regulation. The number registered by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau totaled more than 6.2 million bags. However, after further investigation by dispatched personnel and reports from various foreign firms, the actual number exceeded the registered number. After detailed research by the bureau, a solution was drafted and submitted to the municipal government for approval. The municipal government believes that the influx of foreign rice has a significant impact on rural areas, and also considers the importance of the people's food supply. The solution proposed by the Social Affairs Bureau will be submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. According to information obtained by the Dagong News Agency, the solution includes: (1) Unregistered foreign rice should be ordered to be stopped from being imported by the customs. (2) For No. 3 foreign rice (also known as 60-grain broken rice), the Ministry of Finance should instruct customs offices in various places to increase import tariffs to restrict imports. It is reported that the Executive Yuan will submit this proposal for discussion at the next meeting.

Customs Office Studies Tax Increase Issue

In recent days, the rice market has been discussing the news of a tax increase on foreign rice. One theory is that it will be implemented next month, and another is that it must be passed by the Executive Yuan, ordering the Ministry of Finance to implement it according to the highest principle of the foreign rice import tax previously passed by the Legislative Yuan. A reporter from Dagong News Agency inquired yesterday at the Shanghai office of the Customs Department of the Ministry of Finance. According to Secretary Wei, this matter concerns the national food supply, and whether to increase import taxes on foreign rice is still under careful study. Rumors of a scheduled implementation have not yet received official orders from the Ministry of Finance. However, information obtained by the reporter from other sources suggests that increasing taxes on foreign rice is a demand from all parties and is expected to be realized soon. The authorities, for administrative reasons, fear that prior announcements may cause obstacles, so they are unwilling to easily announce the date of implementation.

Permits Issued for Circulation in Fujian, Guangdong, and Other Provinces

Our country's southwestern provinces, such as Guangdong, Guangxi, and Fujian, except for Zhangzhou and other areas in southern Fujian that produce some rice, generally do not plant rice due to climate conditions and rely entirely on imports of foreign rice. Therefore, the Ministry of Finance will not impose taxes on the import and circulation of foreign rice in Guangdong, Guangxi, and Fujian. If ordering foreign rice from Saigon, a passport must first be obtained for circulation.

Tibet Expert Mr. Payer Arrives in Shanghai 104

Tibetans Granted Him the Privilege of Free Travel

Sir Payer, a friend of the late Dalai Lama, lived in Tibet for 25 years and is known as a Tibet expert. He recently left the British diplomatic community to travel in China and has now arrived in Shanghai. When guests visit him, Mr. Payer asks that they not discuss politics and only describes Tibetan customs and folkways and the beautiful scenery of Lhasa. Mr. Payer lived in Tibet for a long time and returned to his country from Lhasa in 1921. He recently traveled there again for five months, and Tibetans allowed him to travel freely to any place. This kind of privilege is rarely granted to foreigners.

Legislative Committee Member Shi Weihuan Discusses Inspection of Various Exchanges 105

Investigating Methods of Collecting Margin Money

Seeking Opinions on Curbing Yarn Merchant Monopoly

Inspecting the Work of Financial Supervision Commissioners

According to the Central News Agency, the Legislative Yuan has dispatched Legislative Committee members Chen Jianru and Shi Weihuan to Shanghai to investigate the situation of various exchanges in Shanghai, in order to revise the Exchange Law and deliberate on the Ministry of Finance's collection of exchange taxes. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Mr. Shi and Mr. Chen at their hotel and received the following information:

Reviewing Methods of Collecting Margin Money

According to them, they were dispatched to Shanghai to inspect various exchanges because the Legislative Yuan is about to revise the Exchange Law and deliberate on various matters such as the Ministry of Finance's collection of exchange taxes. Therefore, upon arriving in Shanghai, they visited various exchanges one after another and have now completed their mission. The goal is to address the issue of margin money collection, believing that it is indeed necessary for each exchange to collect margin money within a reasonable scope. However, how to collect it and what methods to adopt must be carefully reviewed by the Finance and Industry Committee of the Legislative Yuan to prevent abuses.

Seeking Opinions on Curbing Monopoly

According to reports from various yarn factories, speculators have recently been manipulating the market, causing yarn factories to suffer losses and decline. Therefore, they also sought opinions from various exchanges as much as possible in order to gather them and adopt measures to prevent monopolies and manipulation. There are many opinions from various parties, and after sorting them out and reporting them to Beijing, the government will effectively prohibit them.

Meeting with Supervision Commissioners to Improve Efficiency

The Ministry of Industry and the Ministry of Finance have established exchange supervision commissioners in Shanghai to improve administrative efficiency. This time, they also investigated their work and the confirmation of the title of supervision commissioner, as well as the advancement of their work. In the future, both the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry will implement this work effectively to increase efficiency.

National Government Decides to Levy Transaction Tax

Finally, Mr. Shi said that various exchanges have requested a postponement of the transaction tax. The Legislative Yuan has already discussed and announced various collection methods. As for the date of implementation, it is unknown because the laws stipulate that some laws will be implemented from the date of announcement, while others will be implemented by order of the National Government. Therefore, whether to postpone the collection for one year depends on the National Government because this law belongs to the latter category. Mr. Shi and Mr. Chen are scheduled to take the express train to Beijing on the evening of the 6th to attend the Legislative Yuan meeting and report on everything.

Czech Community to Celebrate President's Birthday Tomorrow 106

Tomorrow is the 85th birthday of Czech President Dr. Masaryk. The Czech embassy in Shanghai will be closed for one day and will hold a celebration at the embassy from 6:00 PM to 8:00 PM. Czech expatriates in Shanghai have been invited to attend. Dr. Masaryk is a famous Czech politician who was born in Hodonín in 1850. He came from humble beginnings and studied philosophy at the University of Vienna. He then devoted himself to writing and worked diligently for the development of Czech culture. He began to be involved in politics in 1890. In his early years, he was a major enemy of radicalism and firmly believed that Austria-Hungary must carry out democratic reforms. Masaryk spared no effort in running for the unification of Czech in Europe during and after the war. Later, he was elected president for his contribution to the country and has been re-elected to this day. His achievements are praised by the Czech people, so they are very excited to celebrate his birthday.

After Completing the Bandit Suppression Work, He Will Build Highways in Four Provinces

Building Highways in Four Provinces

He has made considerable contributions to water conservancy development, road construction, and hygiene implementation. He will soon complete his term and return to Geneva. It is also learned that Dr. Haas will leave Beijing to inspect Shaanxi and other provinces. Whether the League of Nations will continue to send technical liaison personnel to China will depend on whether it is needed.

National Water Conservancy Issues

Regarding national water conservancy issues, a water conservancy committee has been established under the National Economic Council, with Standing Committee Member Kong Xiangxi as the chairman. Various matters are underway. The fundamental solution to the Yellow River is also being compiled into a report by various experts in Beijing. As for the Huai River diversion issue, technical personnel, based on geographical observations, all advocate diverting the Huai River southward into the Yangtze River, which is more suitable than diverting the Huai River into the sea.

China Communications and Other Five Banks Organize Shanghai Commodity Marketing Trust Company 109

Organizing Committee to Discuss Implementation Plan

According to the Central News Agency, the Shanghai Commodity Marketing Trust Company, which will be organized by banks in this city, has taken concrete form. This matter has a significant impact on the flow of funds between the interior and Shanghai, so merchants in the interior also attach great importance to it. The details are as follows:

Capital of One Million

The banks participating in the Shanghai Commodity Marketing Trust Company include the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, the Jiangsu Bank, and the Farmers Bank, with a capital of one million yuan, which is shared equally by the five banks. This matter has been discussed by the banks for a long time and has recently taken concrete form. The articles of association of the company have been decided by the banks, and it will be announced and start operations soon after the banks pay the funds.

Jiangsu Province to Be Piloted First

The banks, in view of the fact that the flow of funds between the interior and Shanghai has been hampered by the sluggish market, have decided to organize the company after several consultations. However, because China is vast, it is difficult to popularize it all at once, so they will start with Jiangsu Province first. Jiangsu Province has a close relationship with Shanghai and is known to be wealthy, making it very convenient for business operations. The Jiangsu Provincial Government has expressed its willingness to do its best to facilitate business operations. After the province has achieved results, it will be promoted to other provinces.

Organizing Committee

Each bank participating in the Shanghai Commodity Marketing Trust Company will nominate one member to form a committee to discuss various implementation plans. Offices will be set up separately in all inland areas of Jiangsu Province to facilitate contact with inland merchants. In the past, inland merchants relied on money shops for funds, but in recent years, the business of money shops has experienced problems, so merchants feel that their economic turnover is not flexible. After the establishment of the company, it will be operated entirely in the form of draft remittance and mortgage, which is not only stable for the banks themselves, but also convenient for merchants.

Promoters of Jiangxi Guangda Porcelain Factory Held a Tea Party in Shanghai the Day Before Yesterday 111

Inviting Guests from All Walks of Life and Raising Funds on the Spot

The Jiangxi Guangda Porcelain Factory has been planned and promoted by Mr. Du Chongyuan and the Jiangxi Provincial Government, and is largely in place. The promoters in Shanghai, Zhang Gongquan, Li Shizeng, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Qian Xinzhi, etc., held a tea party at the World Society on Ferguson Road at 4:00 PM on March 4th, inviting leaders from all walks of life. The guests who attended included Mayor Wu, Cai, Director of the Finance Bureau, Cai Yuanpei, Xu Shiying, Zhang Shizhao, Zhao Jinqing, Li Dachao, Chen Guangfu, Xu Xinliu, Wang Zhixin, Song Ziliang, Chen Liting, Tang Shoumin, Yu Qiaqing, Guo Shun, Nie Lusheng, Fang Yixian, Xiang Kangyuan, Pan Xulun, and more than 40 celebrities from the financial and industrial sectors. First,

Li Shizeng stood up and gave a speech, saying roughly that porcelain is a daily necessity with a large consumption, and it is a business that is very worth running. Now, there is considerable professional talent, Mr. Du Chongyuan, in charge. The Jiangxi Provincial Government is also very enthusiastic about promoting this kind of production business. It is hoped that comrades from the financial and industrial sectors in Shanghai will give special support and enthusiastically invest. Then,

Zhang Gongquan spoke, saying roughly that he was in Shenyang at the time of the September 18th Incident. At that time, all the staff of various agencies in Shenyang fled, and all industrial and commercial sectors stopped business. However, the Zhaoxin Porcelain Factory run by Mr. Du Chongyuan, although adjacent to Beida Camp, the starting point of the incident, continued to work as usual in the factory under the fire of artillery. When he visited the Zhaoxin Porcelain Factory, the order and spirit of the workers in the entire factory were still exceptionally high, and there was no panic at all. After touring the entire factory at that time, he felt very surprised. He deeply admired Mr. Du Chongyuan's fearless spirit and his usual training of employees. At that time, because all the banks in Shenyang were closed, the Zhaoxin Porcelain Factory could not turn around financially, and he had entrusted the Shenyang branch of his bank to help the factory. At that time, it was only out of a kind of emotional effect. He felt that such a factory should not be allowed to close down under any circumstances. As for whether the factory could maintain itself and whether it could repay the debt in the future, he did not consider it at the time. Later, the order in Shenyang gradually recovered, and the Zhaoxin Porcelain Factory continued to operate. According to the Shenyang branch report last year, the debts of the Zhaoxin Factory have been repaid in full one after another, so he felt that Mr. Du Chongyuan's honest attitude in handling affairs was worthy of praise and worthy of introduction. Now, about the process of establishing the Jiangxi Guangda Porcelain Factory, please Mr. Du report.

Du Chongyuan reported that last year, he was introduced by Minister Kong to Jiangxi to discuss with Chairman Tai the establishment of a mechanical porcelain factory. Because the Jiangxi Provincial Government has the greatest determination to develop Jiangxi porcelain, it has adopted his personal opinions as much as possible. After consultation, the first thing was that the Jiangxi Provincial Government allocated 200,000 yuan as a start-up capital. As for the organization, it was completely in accordance with commercial methods. The second thing was that the provincial government guaranteed commercial shares with an annual interest of 6% for three years, that is, if the porcelain factory has no profit to split within three years of opening, the mountain provincial government will be responsible for issuing commercial shares with an interest of 6%. The above two measures have been passed by the Jiangxi Provincial Government Conference, and the share money of 200,000 yuan was allocated by the Mountain Provincial Government in November of last year. He went to Pingjin in January of this year to collect share money from his fellow villagers in the Northeast. In Beiping, it was initiated by Mr. Shen Baifei, Song Shoushan, and Li Xiangzhai. In Tianjin, it was initiated by General Ma Zhanshan, Director Lu Jiqing, and Director Xu Huazhou. It stayed in Pingjin for about a week and raised more than 200,000 yuan in share money. At that time, the cash deposited in the bank was 125,000 yuan. As for Shanghai, before he went to Jiangxi last year, he had a face-to-face meeting with Mr. Shi Liangcai in Hangzhou. Mr. Shi was very concerned about the business he was running and promised to do his best to help and indicated that he would bear the full responsibility for the Shanghai share money. When he arrived in Jiangxi not long ago, Mr. Shi suddenly died in an accident on his way back to Shanghai from Hangzhou. He was deeply grieved, causing the Shanghai share money to suffer a sudden setback. Fortunately, he received the enthusiastic help of Mr. Gongquan and Mr. Yuesheng, so that the fundraising work could continue as before. It is estimated that the share money from all parties has been recognized to be about 700,000 yuan, and there is still a shortage of 300,000 yuan from the original share money. As for the share money from other provinces, according to his plan, he plans to set up branch factories in Changsha and Jinan in the future, so he has asked Chairman Han Xiangfang of Shandong Province and Chairman He Yunqiao of Hunan Province to give special help. Also in Xijing, he has asked Chairman Shao Zhonghui and Director Yang Hucheng to raise funds on his behalf. Although he does not dare to be completely confident in establishing a porcelain factory, he is confident that foreign porcelain factories use mechanical manufacturing and implement scientific management, and their porcelain factory also operates in the same way. As for sales, their porcelain factory mass-produces daily necessities, such as porcelain electrical materials used by transportation agencies, and tableware and ceramic tiles used by ordinary people, which is expected to be in short supply. Moreover, foreign porcelain imports have a 40% tariff, and the Ministry of Finance allows their porcelain factory to sell to various provinces tax-free. With the joint efforts of the government and the people, it is possible to defeat foreign porcelain. The future of the porcelain factory is absolutely optimistic. Today, he is grateful to the guests from all walks of life for taking the time to come, and he is grateful to the masters for initiating the banquet in their busy schedules. He will briefly report on the origin of the preparation of the Guangda Porcelain Factory and the fundraising process, and express his gratitude.

Qian Xinzhi said that in the spring of 1931, Mr. Du Chongyuan once raised new shares for the Liaoning Zhaoxin Porcelain Factory and raised tens of thousands of yuan in Shanghai. In the autumn of the same year, the September 18th Incident happened, and the shareholders in Shanghai thought that this share capital must be completely lost. Later, Mr. Du Chongyuan, in view of the fact that the Zhaoxin Porcelain Factory had lost its hope for development under the pressure of foreign forces, soon after the incident, he took out all the share money that Shanghai could invest in from the Liaoning Zhaoxin Porcelain Factory and returned it to the Shanghai shareholders. He deeply admired Mr. Du's integrity and was willing to supplement a little personal opinion in this tea party.

Mayor Wu inquired that he had been to Liaoning and visited the Zhaoxin Porcelain Factory run by Mr. Du Chongyuan. The products in his factory are not what they usually see in Shanghai. They are completely ordinary daily necessities, and most of them are sold to various rural areas, so he felt that the failure of Jiangxi porcelain to develop in the past was actually biased towards art. Its finished products are for a very small number of people to buy as antiques, so each piece of fine porcelain is very expensive and has no practical use. And a delicate ornament is always treasured and not easily damaged, so that the sales of the products are extremely narrow, and all electrical materials and daily necessities are completely made of foreign porcelain, which makes the leakage of funds more and more serious. It is really heartbreaking. The first reason why Mr. Du Chongyuan succeeded is that he obtained the largest outlet for sales and abandoned the manufacture of art for people to appreciate. The second reason why Mr. Du Chongyuan succeeded is that he worked sincerely and earnestly based on what he had learned. He did not aim too high, did not do ideal work that was not easy to do temporarily, and specialized in doing things that were easy to achieve and easy to succeed. He thought that with Mr. Du's past experience, it was most suitable to develop the porcelain industry in Jiangxi in terms of people. When the porcelain factory starts work in the future, all porcelain electrical materials used by government agencies can be ordered from the porcelain factory, and the social necessities can be supplied by the porcelain factory. There are too many opportunities for development in terms of sales. The business is bound to be successful. He very much hopes that the comrades from all walks of life and those who intend to invest will pay attention together and help each other.

Xu Junren gave a speech that his friend Chen Dazhang had previously established a porcelain company in Jingdezhen. According to his friend's experience, if he bought a machine for 5,000 yuan, he could produce 6,000 pieces of porcelain a day. If he used twelve workers and manufactured by hand, he could only produce 300 pieces a day. How can Chinese handicraft resist foreign porcelain? In the future, if the mechanical porcelain factory in Jiangxi is established, its output will definitely create an amazing number in porcelain production, so he is eager for its early success, etc. Finally,

Li Shizeng proposed that on the spot, he asked the supporters to write down the amount of money they would raise and to be responsible for paying the shares within three months. It was estimated that more than 100,000 yuan of share money was raised on the spot. The remaining share money of 200,000 yuan was shared equally by the masters of the tea party today. The guests and hosts toasted each other and dispersed happily until 7:00 PM.

Former Police Chief Wen Chaoji's Enduring Legacy 114

Offenders Must Be Released Within 24 Hours

What most benefited the citizens and made them forever grateful was that, from the beginning of his tenure, Mr. Wen immediately issued an order to all subordinate police stations and judicial departments, stipulating that, henceforth, regardless of the type of offender, they must all be interrogated and submitted for review within 24 hours. Those who could be released should be released, and those who needed to be transferred should be transferred, so as to avoid the suffering of the people being unjustly detained. Organizational Methods of Various Marketing Cooperatives (Continued) 117

Mr. Stephen's Speech

Here is an example to examine the advantages and disadvantages of the centralized and federated models. In Michigan, USA, there is the Michigan Potato Growers Exchange, a federated potato marketing cooperative. In Minnesota, there is the Minnesota Potato Growers Exchange, a centralized potato marketing cooperative. The central cooperative of the centralized model has storage rooms, while in the federated model, each cooperative has its own. In the federated cooperative of Michigan, if a new method of grading is invented, the head office can only send instructors to advise the branches to implement it, but if the branches do not agree, it will not take effect, and leaving the cooperative is very free. However, this is not the case with the cooperative in Minnesota. Whenever a new policy is to be implemented, it only needs to be approved by more than half of the directors to order the district offices to comply. It will not be changed due to the disagreement of some members. If there is disagreement, the only option is to withdraw from the cooperative. However, with regard to individual withdrawal, once withdrawn, there is no opportunity to cooperate and market on their own, as in the federated model. The opportunity for marketing cooperation disappears because all its powers are governed by the central cooperative. This is not the case with the federated cooperative. If it withdraws, its organization still exists and can be re-integrated to carry out marketing activities without being affected.

The trademark of the potatoes produced by the Michigan Cooperative is a triangular symbol. The ownership of this trademark belongs to the federated cooperative. The products of all branches must be of equivalent grade before the triangular trademark can be applied. This trademark already has considerable credibility in society. Several branches have withdrawn because the restrictions of the federated cooperative were too strict, and marketed separately. As a result, the results were poor, and they rejoined. This is indeed an excellent way to teach a lesson to the cooperative, and at the same time, it does not affect the entire cooperative business due to the withdrawal of a few branches. The centralized cooperative in Minnesota is different. In the area of the cooperative, the soil types in each district are different. One district is sandy soil, so potatoes mature very early and can be sold at a good price. The potatoes produced in other districts with clay soil need to be stored and sold gradually. Not only is the selling price not as good as those that mature early, but also the funds required for the special construction of warehouses are quite large. Therefore, the farmers in the sandy soil area are dissatisfied with the average calculation of the selling price and the warehouse construction funds that are not necessary for themselves and must be reluctantly borne, and feel that the treatment is unfair. The potatoes in the sandy soil area are sold early because they mature early, and there is no need for special warehouse equipment, and those that mature early ask for early settlement to avoid additional interest. However, the cooperative is afraid that early settlement will affect the financial turnover of the entire cooperative, and does not allow the request. Therefore, the farmers in the sandy soil area expressed dissatisfaction with the cooperative. Some say, why not divide the members of the two districts with different natures into two groups and price them separately? However, because the centralized model takes the policy that everything must be decided by the board of directors, and the directors are elected separately by each district, the clay soil area occupies the majority in the area of the cooperative, so most of the directors are thinking for the benefit of the clay soil area. This method is difficult to achieve. In this situation, if in the Michigan Federated Cooperative, the members of the sandy soil area, if they are not satisfied, can withdraw from the federation in an organized way and still cooperate in marketing. However, the centralized model is not possible, because after withdrawal, they become individuals and lose the opportunity to cooperate in marketing. The final result of the Minnesota Cooperative is that some members requested early settlement without success, felt that the treatment was unfair, and requested to withdraw from the cooperative. However, due to the restrictions of the contract, they were helpless. These branch cooperatives launched a major attack on the cooperative. Later, because they could not bear it, they withdrew from the cooperative regardless of the constraints of the law. Therefore, the burden on the remaining members of the cooperative to bear the entire equipment increased. As a result, the remaining members also expressed dissatisfaction, leading to the failure and disintegration of the centralized cooperative. In addition to Minnesota, there is also a potato centralized cooperative in Maine, in the east, which also failed. The federated cooperative in Michigan can still operate to this day, and the life of the California Fruit Marketing Cooperative, a federated cooperative, is also very long, because the organization of the federated model is relatively free. (To be continued)

The Drought Relief Association Reports Detailed Records of Relief Distribution in Liyang and Ten Other Counties 119

The Drought Relief Association of Various Provinces yesterday received a detailed relief distribution report from Cheng Yiqing, the Jiangsu Inspection Director of the Association, on the relief distribution in Liyang, Lishui, and ten other counties in Jiangsu. The report listed the severity of the disaster, the number of households investigated, the distribution of relief funds, and the levels of distribution in great detail. However, the disaster was widespread and the funds were meager, so the principle of saving the dying rather than the poor was adopted, and strict deductions were made. However, it was still a drop in the bucket and difficult to universalize. Spring relief is approaching, and the time between the exhaustion of the old harvest and the arrival of the new is particularly critical. If the relief is not increased, the number of deaths will inevitably increase day by day. Benefactors at home and abroad, after carefully examining the details of the disaster in the table, will surely know that emergency relief cannot be delayed. Feelings will arise, and they will take off their clothes and share their food, not shirking their responsibility. Saving a person's life is better than building a seven-story pagoda, and the merits are truly immeasurable. Detailed list of the disaster in each county is as follows:

The entire territory of Liyang County suffered a complete crop failure. In addition, sericulture has gone bankrupt in the past three years, and ten houses out of ten are empty. Countless people have sold their sons and daughters, and most of the able-bodied men have fled. The food is completely bran and wild vegetables for sustenance. It should be listed as a particularly severe disaster area. Lishui County's entire county is divided into five districts, with the first and second districts being the most severe, the third and fourth districts being the next most severe, and the fifth district being less affected. Except for the fifth district, it is generally the same as Liyang, but its food is mainly weathered stones. There are deaths every day, and it should be listed as a particularly severe disaster area. Gaochun County's entire territory is divided into five districts. Except for the second district, all the fourth and fifth districts are affected, which is the most severe. Three-fifths of the third district is the most severe, and three-fifths of the first district is the next most severe. After investigation and deduction, there are more than 121,100 disaster victims, including men, women, old, and young, who cannot be further reduced. More than 70,000 people cannot survive without relief. The food relies entirely on four types: weathered stones, elm bark, buckwheat hulls, and wild vegetables. There are more deaths in the fourth and fifth districts, and the rest are also pale and emaciated, a tragic sight. It should be listed as the most severe disaster area. Jiangpu County's entire territory is mountainous and has always been barren. The entire county is divided into five districts. The first and second districts, bordering the river, still have a thin harvest. The third, fourth, and fifth districts are mountainous, with the fourth district being particularly large, accounting for half of the county, and the most severely affected. There are no grains harvested, and they are now filling their stomachs with grass roots. There have been deaths. Child murder cases due to hunger have occurred repeatedly in Tangquan Town. It should be listed as the most severe disaster area. Jurong County's entire county is divided into five districts, with the third and fourth districts being the most severe and the first, second, and fifth districts being lighter. The people are displaced and there are deaths every day. The tragic situation is unbearable to witness. The food is mostly wild vegetables, sugar bran, and weathered stones. It should be listed as a severe disaster area. Jintan County's entire county is divided into six districts, all of which have suffered from drought, especially the second, fifth, and sixth districts, which are as miserable as Jurong. It should be listed as a severe disaster area. Yixing County's entire county is divided into eight districts, with the fourth, fifth, sixth, and seventh districts being the most severe, the first and eighth districts being the next most severe, and the second and third districts being lighter. In the most severe districts, the tragic situation is similar to Jurong and Jintan. Selling sons and daughters is often heard, and countless people have fled the country. It should be listed as a severe disaster area. Zhenjiang County's entire county is divided into seven districts. Except for the seventh district, which is not affected, the (3), (5), and (6) districts are the most severe, and the (1), (2), and (4) districts are the next most severe. The most severe districts are indeed miserable. It should be listed as a secondary severe disaster area. Jiangning County's new second, new third, and new sixth districts are all affected, and most of the rest are partial disasters. Danyang County's entire county is divided into eight districts, with the third and seventh districts being the most severe, the fourth, fifth, and sixth districts being the next most severe, and the first, second, and eighth districts being the next most severe. The Association has allocated three times relief funds to Jiangsu Province, totaling 100,000 yuan, which were handed over to the investigation and distribution director for distribution. According to the list in this table, 59,672 yuan has been allocated and distributed, and there are still more than 40,000 yuan that have not been allocated. We previously requested an additional allocation of 10,000 yuan for Lishui and 8,000 yuan for Gaochun. If approved, the remaining amount would be approximately 22,000 yuan. According to Deputy Director Li, the amount is used to support the lighter disaster areas of Wujin, Luhe, Yizheng, and Jiangdu. The number of deficits may not be too many. However, spring relief is extremely urgent. What we have seen and heard makes us feel that if we do not increase the spring relief in the seven counties listed above, the number of deaths will inevitably increase day by day. The Bureau of International Trade Introduces Domestic Products 120

Promoting Pine Nut Oil and Kaolin to Overseas Markets

According to the Bureau of International Trade, in recent years, European and American import and export merchants have often sent letters to the Bureau requesting the introduction and purchase of domestic products, and domestic manufacturers have also sent letters to the Bureau requesting the introduction and promotion of foreign countries. In today's depressed economic climate, the only way to rescue domestic manufacturers is to expand the sales of domestic products. The recent requests from foreign merchants for introductions are described below:

The United States Needs Pine Nut Oil

Pine nuts are brown triangular seeds grown on pine trees. When the shell is removed, the inside contains soft kernels with a fragrant aroma, which is generally recognized as a tonic that can prolong life, increase muscle, and is commonly used to make sweets. In medicine, it can be used to treat coughs and constipation. Now, scientists have found that pine nut oil is extremely rich in vitamin A and can be used to manufacture a medicine. The World Produce Trading Company of the United States has sent a letter requesting this pine nut oil. If you are in the business of this product, you can send a letter to the Bureau's Guidance Department for introduction.

Dutch Dye Factories Need Kaolin

Kaolin is a pure silica, a natural weathered porcelain clay. When pure, it is a fine, clean white powder. Its main uses are as a raw material for making porcelain and sizing paper and yarn. The number exported from Shanghai every year is quite large. The Frankentant Dyeworks of the Netherlands has sent a letter requesting an introduction to kaolin merchants for the purpose of trading. If you wish to promote this product overseas, you can send a letter to the Bureau for introduction.

Three Women Found Hanged

Yesterday, she quarreled with her husband, Wang Si (formerly a laborer), because she had no money to buy rice. Resentful, she took her own life by hanging herself with her belt. The verification was reported by local security Zhang Fengqi. Another Yangzhou woman, Du Hu, aged 64, who lived at 31 Xiyangjiazhai, Pudong, had been a widow for many years and relied on her son, Du Zhonghao, for a living. Recently, Zhonghao suddenly lost his job, and the family's expenses were in a panic. They pawned their belongings day by day. Du Hu thought that the future was long and life was worse than death, so she hanged herself the night before while her son and daughter-in-law were asleep. When she was discovered yesterday morning, it was too late. The verification was reported by local security Lu Shunlong. A nameless male corpse of about 30 years old, wearing a black cotton jacket, blue cloth pants, bean-colored thread socks, and leather shoe-style cotton shoes, was found in the Suzhou River at the Xinqiao of the Shamban Factory in North Shanghai yesterday morning. The corpse floated there and it was not known where it came from. To Be Sent to Court Today for Interrogation

Xu Meiying, a woman from Jiangwan, is 28 years old and has a certain beauty. She used to be a worker in the Lake Silk Store. Five years ago, after becoming acquainted with Gu Xiaodi, a copper craftsman who repairs cars, she changed her career and became a hostess in the Dajing Opera Theater in the rooftop garden of the New World Department Store on Nanjing Road, and became known as the "Hot Water Thermos and Glass Cup." She lived with her lover at 88 Jin Shenfu Road, the front room on the third floor of the Yuanshenchang Porcelain Shop. At 9:00 AM on the first day of this month, Gu Xiaodi went to work at the Yuanheng Auto Repair Company on Lafayette Road. Xu was sleeping alone at home when a man in short clothes broke into her home, untied the trousers belt around Xu's waist, strangled Xu to death, and stole a gold bracelet worth more than 400 yuan, three gold rings, and dozens of yuan in cash. At noon, her lover, Gu Xiaodi, returned home for lunch and discovered the incident, reporting it to the French Concession Police, who transported the body to the coroner's office. The next day, he reported it to the Second Special Court, which sent personnel to verify the incident and ordered the body to be collected. At the same time, the police ordered all the detectives to strictly arrest the fugitive murderer and bring him to justice for interrogation. He was taken to the police station for interrogation. According to Xue, he admitted to going to steal property, and because Xu resisted, he strangled her to death. It is also rumored that Xue was the lover of the deceased and had a physical relationship with her. He wanted to marry Xu and asked her to divorce Gu, but Xu refused, so he resented her and killed her. Whether this is true remains to be verified. The police are currently summoning the coroner and the second landlord, Wang Nianzu, for identification and conducting a thorough investigation. He will be sent to the Second Special Court for interrogation this morning.

According to Laisilai's wife, the deceased was usually very amiable, and there were never any conflicts between husband and wife. This sudden suicide was caused by nerve confusion due to drunkenness. After the detectives finished their investigation, they transported the body to the sanitation office to report it for examination.

Chamber of Commerce Cables Ministry of Transportation to Stop Foreign Ships from Sailing Inland 127

Jilaiyang Shipping Company's Ships Enter Fujian's Inland Ports

Not Only Infringing on Navigation Rights But Also Violating Treaties

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday sent a telegram to the Ministry of Transportation in Nanjing, stating: "To the esteemed Ministry of Transportation: On the 4th of this month, we received a letter from the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association, a member of our Chamber, stating that the Zhen'an Shipping Company reported that the Kthel Moller ship of the Jilaiyang Shipping Company had loaded cargo and sailed to Xiuyu, Fuqing, Xinghua, and other ports in Fujian Province. These ports are all inland ports where foreign ships have not previously operated. Currently, the Fuan and Fuping ships operate on these routes and are sufficient to meet the needs. Now, foreign ships, in violation of treaty provisions, are loading passengers and cargo and rashly sailing there, intentionally infringing on navigation rights. Furthermore, we have heard that the company also intends to send the Margaret Moller and Chrhtine Moller ships. If this is not stopped, the consequences will be endless. We urge the Chamber to promptly forward this to the relevant authorities and strictly prohibit it to protect national rights. We, the Chamber, have investigated and confirmed that Xiuyu and other ports in Fujian Province are inland ports where foreign ships are not allowed to operate according to treaties. It is imperative to stop this. In addition to sending a telegram to the Ministry of Transportation to order the relevant authorities to pay attention and stop this trend, we are sending this letter. We respectfully hope that you will investigate and approve our joint support to achieve the prohibition and alleviate the situation." According to this, our inland ports are not permitted for foreign ships to navigate is specified in treaties. Xiuyu, Fuqing, Xinghua, and other ports in Fujian Province are all our inland ports. Jilaiyang Shipping Company has dared to send foreign ships to load passengers and cargo, which not only infringes on our navigation rights but also violates the treaties. To prevent this trend, it is necessary to correct this according to the treaties. We are submitting this report by telegram, requesting your esteemed review and prompt negotiation to make a forceful prohibition to maintain the treaties and protect navigation rights, which is in the public interest. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce respectfully submits this with its seal."

Continued Trial of the Wuhua Bank Case 128

After the Shanghai branch of the Guangzhou Wuhua Industrial Trust Bank on Ningbo Road in the Public Concession and the Baxianqiao branch in the French Concession both collapsed on August 21st of last year, depositors and creditors, including Chu Longgen, Chen Xianji, Luo Lihua, Shi Pengfei, Du Zhiji, Shi Bilong, Shen Peng, Zhou Delin, Wang Fuji, Pan Yuanji, and others, jointly hired lawyers to file a lawsuit in the Second Special District Court Criminal Division, accusing Fan Shaoliang, Wang Jian'e, Ye Haitian, and Wu You San, the deputy managers of the Wuhua branches, Xie Shunzhi and Tang Songshan, the assistant managers, and Tang Shoumin and Chen Bingqian, the consultants, of fraud and breach of trust. The lawsuit alleged that the bank had not registered with the Ministry of Finance of the National Government and had rashly opened for business, using advertisements of five-year and ten-year plans to solicit deposits with high interest rates. The court, after receiving the lawsuit, opened hearings multiple times with Judge Zhang Chaozuo presiding to summon the defendants. The defendants were defended by lawyers Jiang Yiping, Hua Maosheng, Wu Kaisheng, and others. Huang Linsheng, the authorized representative sent by the Guangzhou head office to Shanghai to be responsible for the liquidation, was summoned to the court for questioning. The debate was concluded on January 12th of this year, and the sentencing was scheduled for January 19th. However, the presiding judge stated that the organization of the branch's board of directors and whether the defendants had any shares were not yet clear, so the conclusion of the debate was revoked, and a new debate was scheduled. This was reported previously. Yesterday, Judge Zhang summoned them again in the Criminal Court No. 2. Defendant Tang Shoumin could not attend due to other important matters, and Chen Bingqian could not attend due to illness. The remaining defendants reported with their defense lawyers. After the court opened, the judge announced that the case would be re-examined. First, he asked the plaintiff Chu Longgen about the facts and reasons for the lawsuit. Chu replied that he was accusing the defendants of fraud and breach of trust. They used the bank's name to defraud money and requested that they be punished and the deposits be returned. When asked, the other plaintiffs, Chen Xian and others, stated that their reasons and opinions were the same as Chu's. The court asked defendant Fan Shaoliang, "The court ordered you to submit the organizational structure of the board of directors." Fan replied, "Today, I have asked Lawyer Luo Jiaheng to submit a statement to the court." He also stated, "Headquarters representative Huang Linsheng went to attend the shareholders' meeting because the Guangdong headquarters was holding one, so he could not attend today. I was appointed by the headquarters as the manager of the branch. The assistant manager and the manager are equally responsible, but there is also a supervisor whose responsibility is equal to that of the manager. The assistant managers are hired by the branch manager and reported to the headquarters. The consultants are famous merchants in Shanghai hired by the branch, and their nature is the same as that of consultants. However, consultants and assistant managers do not necessarily have the qualifications for shares, but they can serve. However, among the defendants in the case, it is not clear whether they have shares because many use symbols. I myself have 6,000 yuan of shares. The current state of liquidation is that we originally intended to lease the branch address to Huadong Bank for over 27,000 yuan. This amount could take care of half of the savings portion. However, due to the poor market conditions, Huadong has not yet paid the money after signing the contract, but negotiations are still ongoing." Ye Haitian testified that he had 5,000 yuan of shares and served as assistant manager for ten months. Wang Jian'e testified that he served as the manager of the branch and was appointed by the branch. He had no shares and only worked for two months before the bank collapsed. The savings in the branch's name totaled 13,870 yuan and 86 cents. Wu You San testified that he was appointed by the branch as an assistant manager of the branch and had no shares. Xie Shunzhi testified that he was an assistant manager of the branch and had 3,000 yuan of shares. "My responsibilities and powers as an assistant manager are different from those of ordinary banks in Shanghai. I cannot represent the bank externally, and I cannot interfere with the bank's affairs internally. I only manage business lending affairs." Tang Songshan testified that he served as an assistant manager of the branch and had no shares. "I am only responsible for the business part. I have no power to sign externally, which is different from other banks. Assistant managers in other banks have power, but Wuhua assistant managers have no power. Moreover, there is also a treasurer above me. It is organized according to the Guangdong bank, so my assistant manager is equal to an employee." Accountant Li Cheng also reported on the progress of the liquidation, saying that after taking over, the books were checked until February 17th, and then handed over to Lawyer Luo Jiaheng for handling. Since only 13,000 yuan of debts owed by people were received after taking over, most of them could not be collected due to poor market conditions. The original plan was to distribute a portion of the debts after leasing the branch address. Now this plan cannot be implemented, so it has been handed over to Lawyer Luo. According to the bank's balance sheet, the assets are more than 420,000 yuan, and the debts are 310,000, so the surplus is still over 110,000 yuan. At this point, the judge ordered Fan Shaoliang to report the progress of the liquidation to the court as soon as possible for verification and instructed Accountant Li to provide a written explanation of all the books for filing. Since the defendants were not all present, it was announced that the case would still need to be investigated and that the debate would not be opened. A further hearing was scheduled, and the court was adjourned.

Method for Changing Trains and Supplementing Ticket Prices 130

The Traffic Departments of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways have stipulated the method for passengers who change from ordinary trains to express trains to supplement their ticket prices. Yesterday, a special notice was issued to station staff: "It is common for passengers on fast or slow trains to transfer to express trains when the former give way at stations to the latter, especially when both are traveling in the same direction. The method for supplementing the fare is now stipulated as follows: (1) If a passenger changes trains, they should first declare it to the conductor or ticket inspector of the train and pay the express surcharge for all miles from the station where the transfer takes place to the final destination on the ticket. The ticket inspector should also note this on the supplemental ticket. (2) If a passenger changes trains without declaring it, they should pay the express train surcharge for all miles between the origin and destination stations on the ticket."

To the esteemed Editor: I am writing to you regarding a news item in yesterday's news column about the enthusiastic recruitment efforts of the various aviation patriotism teams. After taking office as captain, he immediately convened a meeting of the executive and supervisory committee and immediately decided that all members of the executive and supervisory committee would be the deputy captains and the managers of each line would be the team members, and expanded the recruitment of members to all industries and solicited aviation patriotism donations from outside." Upon investigation, I resigned from the chairmanship of the association in December of last year, and Mr. Wang Huaiquan was publicly recommended to succeed me, and reports were submitted separately. Subsequently, I received a letter from the Shanghai Recruitment Team General of the China Aviation Association, inviting me to be the captain of the 212th team, and a letter of appointment was attached. Since I had resigned from the chairmanship of the association earlier and generally did not consult on association affairs, I asked Chairman Wang to take on the position of captain and transferred the letter of appointment and other documents to the association. All implementation methods are handled by Chairman Wang. What your newspaper reported does not conform to the facts. I urge you to correct it immediately. With best wishes. Sincerely, Cai Run Shen, March 5th.

Spring and Autumn — (Yan Xinquan)

Tidbits 141

Miss Wang is the daughter of a wealthy family in the village and has a strong love for fashion. One day, Miss Wang's friend, Ms. So-and-so, told me: "Look! Miss Wang's eyebrows have become so thin recently! She plucked them with tweezers; when she was plucking them, she almost cried out in pain several times." This can be said to be a kind of punishment suffered for fashion!

Five years ago, when Miss Lu was teaching at × Girls' School, she saw that the students were wasting their time, so she often warned them with words such as: "Every moment of time is worth a thousand gold." "An inch of time is worth an inch of gold..." But today, five years later, Miss Lu has changed a lot. Not to mention anything else, the time she spends on decoration every day is really astonishing.

Wanli Bridge 142

— Lu Jia

Speaking of the two words "Wanli" (ten thousand li), it gives us a sense of grandeur. For example, the Great Wall is so great! In our imagination, a long snake-like city winding continuously will be reflected. And here, I want to talk about a bridge.

Wanli Bridge, this name seems to be heard from time to time, but it is also a very familiar noun in the north. This bridge, in Shangcheng County, Henan Province, is built of stone and is 18 li long. Naturally, calling it Wanli Bridge is to describe its length, and Chinese people are the most fond of exaggeration.

Although the bridge is 18 li long, the river is not necessarily wide, so two-thirds of the bridge is on dry land, like a small mountain. The bridge surface is very wide. On this side, you step on the stone steps and slowly go up, and the bridge also rises little by little. Walking to the top of the bridge, there are four small tea pavilions for pedestrians to rest their feet. Those who are hurrying to get on the road are sweating and panting when they reach the top, which is very exhausting. From this, it can be seen that the length of this bridge is indeed enough to amaze us. Usually, there is nothing that can be used for transportation in this place, only goat carts, but it is very dangerous to ride in this kind of cart.

Based on my shallow knowledge, I feel that there is no bridge in China more magnificent than this Wanli Bridge. Unfortunately, I don't know in which dynasty this bridge was built.

Yuanbao Basket 143

— Hu Xidan

The term "yuanbao" sounds very pleasant, but its shape is quite peculiar. With its two ends raised and its body slanting, people have never considered it a noble item. They look down on it, so its use is merely as an accessory when housewives go to the market. However, it is unwilling to play a humble role. It doesn't hold expensive items like meat and fish; it only carries light items like tofu and small white fish. Housewives also place leftover silver coins and copper coins in it, which shows that it is relatively pampered, although perhaps its constitution is indeed a bit weak. But we should know that it didn't do this kind of work hundreds of years ago! As the saying goes, "Every profession produces its top talent." Its ancestors often accompanied top scholars as the second life for those who went to take the imperial exams. Let me tell you about it:

During the Song dynasty, the court heavily promoted the practice of selecting scholars for advancement through examinations. After the provincial exams were completed, many rushed to the capital to participate in the palace exam. Their luggage and furniture, besides bedding, swords, and examination baskets, mostly included a yuanbao basket with auspicious patterns. It is said that the styles at that time were somewhat pointed, probably to symbolize "rising step by step"! The yuanbao basket's status today is not the same as in the past, so it's no wonder it can't help but feel sentimental about the past. Some people also say that the current yuanbao basket is transformed from the old one, but whether this is true remains to be verified.

Ma Bao 144

— Zhou Zixin

The name "Ma Bao" (horse treasure) is quite new to me. It feels unfamiliar and strange. Perhaps most people share the same feeling as I do! After reading the product information for Ma Bao from the San You Industrial Society, I finally understood that it is a precious medicine for treating diseases.

It is said that Ma Bao is produced in the remote border regions, where horses are bred. These horses, in the open wilderness, occasionally eat unique herbs. Their daily feed then no longer digests properly and accumulates in their stomachs. The horses themselves also receive the spiritual energy of the mountains and rivers, and the essence of the sun and moon. The accumulated food, through these two layers of blessing, eventually forms a hard substance, neither stone nor bone. This hard substance, as if cursed, blocks the horse's food intake, causing the horse to be neither hungry nor full all day long. During this period, due to the lack of food, the horse's fur gradually thins and falls out, like wet fur, and eventually the horse loses its life.

The quality of Ma Bao is distinguished mainly by its color and weight. It is said that the best quality is pure white, heavy, with little sandy texture, and with a solid core. However, this is not easy for non-experts to discern. Ma Bao is said to be effective in treating spitting blood, phlegm obstruction, and other conditions. Perhaps this is why it is so expensive!

Poor animal—the horse—eats unique herbs, receives the spiritual energy of the mountains and rivers, and absorbs the essence, only to lose its life. Yet, we people regard the thing that caused its death (Ma Bao) as a precious medicine. This makes me constantly question and unable to understand!

White Cloud 145

— (Feifei)

I wish I could transform into a white cloud, floating freely and comfortably in the boundless sky all day long, coming and going as I please, without any restraint. I could travel to the ends of the earth without anyone interfering with me. Not to mention people not daring to interfere, even the moon and the sun couldn't interfere with me.

When happy, I would chase and frolic with the raging tides, or hold hands, jump, and dance. Otherwise, I would flirt with the charming spring flowers or confide in the melancholic autumn moon. Or, I would play with the shy stars in the silent night sky.

When tired, I would casually rest on the peaks of high mountains, looking down and quietly listening to the roaring tides of the ocean.

When unhappy, I would immediately put on a stern face, feel a coldness in my heart, and condense into a torrential rain, washing away the ugly hearts of the world!

Alas! White cloud, white cloud, when will I ever be able to transform into a carefree white cloud? (Response)

Local Customs

A Retrospective of the Shanghai-Gaoqiao Route 146

— Zhen Lü

The Shanghai Pier of the Shanghai Ferry Company has recently been moved from the Bund on Nanjing Road (commonly known as the Copper Man Pier) to the Bund on Beijing Road. The newly built double-decker pier has set a new record in the history of Chinese architecture, which deserves everyone's attention. The main route of this city ferry is from Shanghai to Gaoqiao—a town in Pudong. It has only been extended to Wusong in the past year or two.

Although Gaoqiao's town diameter is less than three li at its longest point, it is the hometown of the famous contemporary figure Du Yuesheng, and officials often come and go. It also produces many authoritative figures in the construction industry (Pudong has always been famous for producing skilled carpenters and foremen). It can also promote various new facilities in the locality. It is also conveniently located along the Huangpu River, making it suitable as the tail end of Shanghai's crowded residential areas. In addition, in recent years, a seaside bathing beach has been set up on the coast three or four li from the town, which can stimulate the true interest in life for Western expatriates in Shanghai and a group of new figures. —With both outstanding people and a favorable environment, the traffic on that route has naturally made great progress and is still in its ascendant!

The Shanghai-Gaoqiao route has achieved today's success and has a simple history that can be recorded, proving the speed of its progress and reflecting the huge waves of Shanghai's prosperity affecting the areas near Shanghai. It is adapting to the needs and geographical advantages.

Twenty-five years ago, residents of Gaoqiao had to take a sailing boat to Shanghai, which took four or five hours. After more than fifty li of the swaying river journey, it was like the situation two years ago when one had to take a long ferry to go directly from Gaoqiao to Wusong. Therefore, unless absolutely necessary, Gaoqiao people would never go to Shanghai.

Later, in Donggou, about twelve li from Gaoqiao, there was the Donggou Embankment Bureau in the area. Mr. Zhu Futian, the director, pioneered a small steamship line running from Donggou to Shanghai. Most Gaoqiao people then did not hesitate to pay for a rickshaw to take the route through Donggou to catch the steamer, seeking its stability, speed, and convenience.

A year or two later (about twenty years ago), a local gentleman from Gaoqiao, Mr. Sun, independently established the Tongxing Small Steamer Company. He built a pier less than three li from the town, at Tiandengtou, a slight advancement into the Gaoqiao boundary river port. In Shanghai, he still used the Copper Man Pier where Gaoqiao boats had always docked, which was only recently replaced. The small steamer ran six or seven times a day, and one of the trips always towed a sailing boat, carrying heavy goods. The sailing boat was moored on the Pujiang River at the 16th Pier in Nanshi, so that passengers could conveniently handle goods nearby. The direct ferry service from Gaoqiao to Shanghai started from this point. The old-fashioned sailing boats naturally became obsolete.

After Gaoqiao was incorporated into Shanghai Municipality, the city ferry began to operate and also docked at Donggou. The city ferry's Gaoqiao pier was built on the Pujiang River bank—at the furthest point of Tiandengtou, making it even more convenient for the steamer not to enter the port. It fairly allowed the old steamer—now named Heji—to continue operating as usual, retaining its old pier until now. (To be continued)

Little Western Paradise 147

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 10: Imprudent Young Man Reveals Wealth in Front of a Young Woman; Coveting the Wall Gap for a Sexual Affair Causes Illness and Damages Integrity

Madam Zhu Hu said: "I heard it, I heard Mr. Zhang say it several times. You tell me to activate my mind a bit, how do I activate it?" Zhang Jiefu couldn't help but chuckle, thinking that he was originally too honest. With such a muddle-headed woman, he should just speak in riddles with her. How could she understand? He raised his head and thought for a moment, and said with a smile: "Money is very hard to come by, you should know that." Madam Hu said: "Yes! That's what I'm saying too. How can the money be mine if I just activate my mind?" Zhang Jiefu said: "This is not a lie. The reason why this Mr. Jia wants to marry someone is because he is too lonely and wants someone to accompany him. If..." He felt it difficult to continue speaking, and coughed lightly twice. But he needed money just as much as Madam Zhu Hu did. He had his own plan, and this plan had to be helped by Jia Duocai. So, how could he not make this happen? So he encouraged his own courage, looked at Yueying, and then said to Madam Hu: "Since you are already willing to give your daughter to this Mr. Jia." Madam Hu nodded and said: "I'm more than willing to give her to such a rich man!" Zhang Jiefu said: "Then that's easy. You two are willing to give and willing to take, so your daughter will be his family member sooner or later. Why not just..." Saying this, he paused and smiled again. Madam Zhu Hu looked at him with her eyes rolling, still not understanding what he meant. But Miss Yueying understood somewhat. It was definitely not something good to hear, so she frowned and said to Jiefu: "Mr. Zhang, we are all pitiful people and don't understand anything. If you tell us to do something that we can do, we will definitely do it without saying a second word. If we can't do it, please forgive us, Mr. Zhang. How would we dare to say anything?" (149)

Royal Fragrance Drifting Record 148

— Original by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

They were not originally on this yellow train with us. They were loaded onto the second train behind, along with the soldiers. The Empress Dowager was initially very interested in them, but after hearing them a few times, she said she was tired of them. At this time, she had completely forgotten that there was this group of people on the troop train behind. So when Li Lianying came to report this matter to her, she just nodded vaguely and said nothing.

After passing that long line of prostrating officials, the platform ended—they knelt across the entire platform. At that time, Tianjin was not very lively. A little further away from the station, all that could be seen on both sides were earthen mound-like graves and boundless fields. The Empress Dowager was no longer in the mood to lean against the window and gaze idly, and she returned to her throne as before. At this time, the speed of the train gradually increased again. I estimated from the degree of vibration of the vehicles that it was probably running faster now than before arriving in Tianjin. We actually all hoped so. Even the Empress Dowager did not show any dissatisfaction with the increased vibration of the vehicles. It was as if there was some terrible demon chasing us from behind, making us unable to escape. The scenery along the way when we came seemed to have nothing that we did not like to see. Now that we were returning, the scenery was still the same as it was more than ten days ago, but when we saw it, we actually felt some fear.

Our royal train soon arrived at Fengtai. Although there were also many officials kneeling to greet the Holy Presence, the Empress Dowager would not pay attention to them. Li Lianying would certainly not come to report to the Empress Dowager again. There was no reason for the train to slow down again, it just glanced over and passed. But once past Fengtai, Beijing was near. The speed of the train finally gradually decreased, letting it slowly flow towards Yongdingmen. That was where the Empress Dowager boarded the train when she left Beijing. (260)

Page 13

Sports News

Executive Yuan Meeting Passes Seven Items for National Games Implementation 149

To be held alternately in the capital and various provinces and cities

Nanjing, 5th—The seven items for the implementation of the National Games were passed by the Executive Yuan meeting on the 5th. (1) In order to promote national sports, the National Games will be held once every two years, alternately in the capital and suitably selected locations in various provinces and cities (i.e., the 5th session in the capital, the 6th session in various provinces and cities, the 7th session in the capital, the 8th session in various provinces and cities, and so on). (2) The location of the Games, other than the capital, should be selected from provinces and cities with convenient transportation and complete sports facilities. The location for the next Games will be determined at the end of each Games held in the capital. (3) Each Games will be held in the autumn. (4) The organizational regulations for each Games will be based on the various items stipulated in the 5th Games held in the capital in 1933, taking into account the circumstances of each location. The Ministry of Education will begin preparations, formulate and announce them, and the expenses required for the Games will be borne by the central and local governments in turn. When held in the capital, the expenses will be submitted by the Ministry of Education to the National Government for approval and issuance. When held in provinces and cities, the expenses will be borne by the local governments. In special circumstances, the Ministry of Education may forward a request for subsidies to the National Government. (6) The Games Preparatory Office will be located in the Ministry of Education in the capital and in the provincial and municipal education administrative organs in various provinces and cities. (7) These measures will be implemented after being submitted by the Ministry of Education to the Executive Yuan for approval.

Li Gongying Retains Shanghai Billiards King Title 151

Shows Skill and Defeats Zhang Yingda

Wins Group A Championship for Three Consecutive Years

Result of the 2nd: 2,000 Points to 1,237

The various competitions organized by the Shanghai Amateur Billiards Association, such as Snooker, Group B, and Group A, concluded last night. Mrs. Zhao Zihui presented the awards. Snooker champion Bellman, runner-up Medina, Group B champion Bailey, runner-up Ye Mouzhuo, and Group A champion Li Gongying, runner-up Zhang Yingda, etc., received their awards amidst applause and retired.

Li Gongying's Superb Artistry

Before the awards were presented, Li Gongying and Zhang Yingda played the final two games of the Group A championship. Li had a 222-point lead from the previous day. At the beginning of his turn, he was incredibly smooth, with huge scores of 74, 68, and 101 in succession, widening the gap significantly. When the unprecedented huge score of 140 was produced, Zhang's position became hopeless. At that time, the beauty of Li's self-landing and layout was truly worth seeing. At the end of the third game, Li had 1,500 points and Zhang had 970 points. Zhang still failed to achieve his goal in the last game. After scoring two large scores of 74 and 63, he encountered unfavorable situations with every shot. At that time, the situation was almost entirely controlled by Li. When Li completed the 2,000-point goal, Zhang had only scored 1,237 points, a difference of 763 points. The large scores of the two are as follows:

Registration Begins for the City's 3rd 20,000-Meter Long-Distance Race 154

Scheduled to be Held in the City Center on the 10th of This Month

Register Now at Daji Road Sports Field

In order to promote sports among the citizens of Shanghai and to make citizens understand the plan to build a Greater Shanghai, the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau has scheduled the 3rd Long-Distance Race to be held in the city center at 9 AM on Sunday, March 10th. Preparations are now complete, and registration will begin immediately, closing on March 9th. The registration location is the Municipal First Public Sports Field on Daji Road. All rules for the race have been submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and implementation. Excerpts are as follows:

Race Rules

Rules for the Shanghai City 3rd Long-Distance Race: Article 1: The purpose of this event is to promote sports among all citizens. Article 2: Any male citizen of this city who is not a professional athlete, aged 16 or older, may participate in the competition. Article 3: The race route will start in front of Fudan University on Xiangyin Road, heading east via Huangxing Road, Kongjiang Road, Mayushan Road, Guanyintang Road, Jungong Road, Puxi Road, Zhayin Road, Minqing Road, Shiguang Road, Guoguang Road, Tonglu Road, Songhu Road, Tonglu Road, Guohua Road, and Fuxi Inner Road, ending at the Municipal Government, a total of 20,000 meters. Article 4: This event will be held at 9 AM on March 10th. Article 5: In addition to the mayor serving as the president and the director of the Education Bureau serving as the vice president, there will be a chief referee and a chief secretary, each one person, and several referees and secretaries, appointed by the director of the Education Bureau. Article 6: All athletes must proceed completely according to the route set by this event. If they run off the route, they should return to the original point and re-run according to the prescribed route. They must not step onto the sidewalk during the race, or be supported by others, or obstruct other athletes from moving forward, and must not ask for guides to lead them. Article 7: The number of winning athletes will be determined based on 15% of the participating athletes (15 athletes will be selected for 100 participants, 30 athletes will be selected for 200 participants, and so on). Article 8: The competition matters are presided over by the chief referee. Athletes may not protest the decision of the chief referee. Article 9: These rules will be implemented after being submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and promulgation.

Notice to Athletes

Notice to Athletes Participating in the Long-Distance Race: (1) Starting Point: Gather in front of Fudan University on Xiangyin Road in the city center for roll call and start. (2) Ending Point: Municipal Government. (3) Route: Start in front of Fudan University on Xiangyin Road, via Huangxing Road, Kongjiang Road, Mayushan Road, Guanyintang Road, Jungong Road, Puxi Road, Zhayin Road, Minqing Road, Shiguang Road, Guoguang Road, Tonglu Road, Songhu Road, Tonglu Road, Guohua Road, and Fuxi Inner Road, ending in front of the Municipal Government, a total of 20,000 meters. (4) Distance: The entire route is divided into ten stages using Arabic numerals 12345678910, with each stage being a distance of 2,000 meters. (5) Qualifications: Any male citizen who is not a professional athlete, aged 16 or older, may register to participate. (6) Registration Location: Municipal First Public Sports Field on Daji Road in Nanshi. (7) Award Ceremony Location: All athletes will gather at the finish line, and after all athletes have arrived, the chief secretary will lead the award ceremony. (8) Race Rules: Athletes must proceed completely according to the route set by this event. If they run off the route, they should return to the original point and re-run according to the prescribed route. They must not step onto the sidewalk during the race, or be supported by others, or obstruct other athletes from moving forward. (9) Security Deposit: Each athlete must pay a security deposit of two small silver coins when registering. The deposit will be returned at the City First Sports Field after the event upon presentation of the race number bib. The deposit will not be returned if the race number bib is lost or if the athlete registers but does not attend. (10) Caretakers: Each athlete should notify their caretaker to wait at the rest area. They are not allowed to ride bicycles and accompany the athletes during the race, disturbing the order.

Two Railways Organize Mountain Climbing Races 159

With Various Preferential Measures

In order to promote national health and encourage travel interest, the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus have scheduled an amateur mountain climbing competition on Mogan Mountain in Zhejiang on the 23rd of this month. Anyone residing in Shanghai, aged between 16 and 40, regardless of gender or nationality, may register to participate. Special preferential measures have been established for participants, with a cost of only under nine yuan per person, including food, accommodation, and transportation. After the competition, if participants wish to stay and tour Mogan Mountain, they can also enjoy the benefit of inexpensive accommodation in the railway hotel for two days, paying only one yuan per person per day within the specified period. In addition, there are also considerable preferential measures for those who wish to watch the competition. Detailed information is available in the Mountain Climbing Handbook, which includes multiple beautifully printed photos of Mogan Mountain scenery and is expected to be published soon. The handbook will be distributed at the Shanghai North Station General Manager's Office, the Information Desk, and the Jing'an Temple Road and Nanshi branch offices. The registration deadline is said to be March 18th. As the spring breeze is warm, it is expected that there will be a large number of participants at that time.

Key Points for Reforming the Standards of Weights and Measures 165

The Executive Yuan convened a meeting of relevant ministries and commissions to revise the standards of weights and measures, as previously reported. The Yuan will soon distribute the details of the meeting and the key points of the reform to relevant agencies and organizations to solicit their opinions. The following is a summary of the detailed review by the Review Committee on the names and definitions of the units in the standards of weights and measures: (A) Participating organizations: Academia Sinica (Ding Xielin), Ministry of Education (Sun Guofeng, Chen Kezhong), Ministry of Industry (Liu Yinfei, Wu Chengluo), Ordnance Administration (Jiang Dashao, Yan Shunzhang), Chinese Physical Society (Hu Gangfu, Yang Zhaozhao), Chinese Institute of Engineers (Yun Zhen). The meeting was chaired by Cen Dezhang of the Executive Yuan, with Ren Shujia as the recorder. (B) Review opinions: Regarding the names of the standards of weights and measures, it was generally agreed that revisions were necessary. It is proposed that the Executive Yuan send the current Weights and Measures Law and the plan proposed by the Physical Society, along with the review opinions of this committee, to relevant government agencies and academic organizations across the country, requesting that they submit their signed opinions before the middle of May, so that the Yuan can convene another review meeting to conduct further research. Regarding the definitions of the standards of weights and measures, it was generally agreed that the regulations for units in the standards of weights and measures should be revised. The main points are as follows: (1) Length and mass should be the basic items of weights and measures. (2) Area, volume (capacity) should be derived items. (3) The meter should be the main unit of length, defined as the distance between the two middle lines at both ends of the original meter bar when the temperature is zero degrees Celsius. (4) The kilogram should be the main unit of mass, defined as the mass of the original kilogram. (5) The square meter should be the unit of area. (6) The cubic meter should be the unit of volume (capacity). (7) The liter should be the applied unit of capacity, defined as the volume occupied by one kilogram of pure water at its maximum density under standard atmospheric pressure. When the required precision does not exceed one part in thirty thousand, one liter can be considered equal to one-thousandth of a cubic meter.
